        <td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">
         <div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0">
          <div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left">
           <a href="/wiki/Alsace#Religion" title="Alsace">
            Religion
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="NavContent" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center;padding-top:0;text-align:left;">
           <center>
            according to
            <br/>
            <a href="/wiki/Concordat_in_Alsace-Moselle" title="Concordat in Alsace-Moselle">

            </a>
            (1801):
            <br/>
            <small>
             <i>
              (including
              <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lorraine_(region)" title="Lorraine (region)">
               Lorraine
              </a>
              )
             </i>
            </small>
           </center>
           <ul>
            <li>
             <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
              Catholic Church
             </a>
             <ul>
              <li>
               <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Strasbourg" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Strasbourg">
                Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Strasbourg
               </a>
               <br/>
               <small>
                (
                <a href="/wiki/Exemption_(church)" title="Exemption (church)">
                 Immediately subject
                </a>
                to the
                <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">
                 Holy See
                </a>
                )
               </small>
               <ul>
                <li>
                 (
                 <a href="/wiki/Prince-Bishopric_of_Strasbourg" title="Prince-Bishopric of Strasbourg">
                  Prince-Bishopric of Strasbourg
                 </a>
                 )
                </li>
               </ul>
              </li>
              <li>
               <i>
                (
                <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lorraine_(region)" title="Lorraine (region)">
                 Lorraine
                </a>
                :
                <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Metz" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Metz">
                 Roman Catholic Diocese of Metz
                </a>
                )
               </i>
              </li>
             </ul>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">
              Protestantism
             </a>
             :
             <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Protestant_Churches_of_Alsace_and_Lorraine" title="Union of Protestant Churches of Alsace and Lorraine">

             </a>
             :
             <ul>
              <li>
               <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">

               </a>
               :
               <ul>

                 </a>
                </li>
               </ul>
              </li>
              <li>

               </a>
               :
               <ul>
                <li>
                 <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformed_Church_of_Alsace_and_Lorraine" title="Protestant Reformed Church of Alsace and Lorraine">
                  Protestant Reformed Church of Alsace and Lorraine
                 </a>
                </li>
               </ul>
              </li>
             </ul>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">

             </a>
             <a href="/wiki/Consistory_(Judaism)" title="Consistory (Judaism)">
              consistories
             </a>
             :
             <ul>

            <img alt="Portal-puzzle.svg" class="noviewer" data-file-height="28" data-file-width="32" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fd/Portal-puzzle.svg/16px-Portal-puzzle.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fd/Portal-puzzle.svg/24px-Portal-puzzle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fd/Portal-puzzle.svg/32px-Portal-puzzle.svg.png 2x" width="16"/>

      <p>
       <b>
        Strasbourg
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'s' in 'sigh'">
            s
           </span>
           <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
            t
           </span>
           <span title="'r' in 'rye'">
            r
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'z' in 'zoom'">
            z
           </span>
           <span title="'b' in 'buy'">
            b
           </span>
           <span title="/ɜːr/: 'ur' in 'fur'">
            ɜːr
           </span>
           <span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">
            ɡ
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       ,
       <small>
        French:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">
         [stʁazbuʁ, stʁas-]
        </a>
       </span>
       ;
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alsatian_language" title="Alsatian language">
        Alsatian
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        Strossburi
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Alemannic_German" title="Help:IPA/Alemannic German">
         [ˈʃd̥ʁɔːsb̥uʁi]
        </a>
       </span>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
        German
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="de">
         Straßburg
        </span>
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">
         [ˈʃtʁaːsbʊɐ̯k]
        </a>
       </span>
       ) is the capital and largest city of the
       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Est" title="Grand Est">
        Grand Est
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_France" title="Regions of France">
        region
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
        France
       </a>
       and is the
       <a href="/wiki/Seat_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Strasbourg" title="Seat of the European Parliament in Strasbourg">
        official seat
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">
        European Parliament
       </a>
       . Located close to the border with
       <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">
        Germany
       </a>
       in the historic region of
       <a href="/wiki/Alsace" title="Alsace">
        Alsace
       </a>
       , it is the capital of the
       <a href="/wiki/Bas-Rhin" title="Bas-Rhin">
        Bas-Rhin
       </a>
       département. In 2014, the city proper had 276,170 inhabitants and both the
       <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg_Eurom%C3%A9tropole" title="Strasbourg Eurométropole">
        Eurométropole de Strasbourg
       </a>
       (Greater Strasbourg) and the
       <a href="/wiki/Arrondissement_of_Strasbourg" title="Arrondissement of Strasbourg">
        Arrondissement of Strasbourg
       </a>
       had 484,157 inhabitants.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-populations_légales_2-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-populations_légales-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Strasbourg's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Area_(France)" title="Metropolitan Area (France)">
        metropolitan area
       </a>
       had a population of 773,347 in 2013 (not counting the section across the border in Germany), making it the ninth largest metro area in France and home to 13% of the Grand Est region's inhabitants. The transnational
       <a href="/wiki/Eurodistrict" title="Eurodistrict">
        Eurodistrict
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg-Ortenau_Eurodistrict" title="Strasbourg-Ortenau Eurodistrict">
        Strasbourg-Ortenau
       </a>
       had a population of 915,000 inhabitants in 2014.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Strasbourg is one of the
       <i>
        de facto
       </i>
       capitals of the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       (alongside
       <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">
        Brussels
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_City" title="Luxembourg City">
        Luxembourg
       </a>
       ), as it is the seat of several European institutions, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">
        Council of Europe
       </a>
       (with its
       <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Human_Rights" title="European Court of Human Rights">
        European Court of Human Rights
       </a>
       , its
       <a href="/wiki/European_Directorate_for_the_Quality_of_Medicines" title="European Directorate for the Quality of Medicines">
        European Directorate for the Quality of Medicines
       </a>
       and its
       <a href="/wiki/European_Audiovisual_Observatory" title="European Audiovisual Observatory">
        European Audiovisual Observatory
       </a>
       ) and the
       <a href="/wiki/Eurocorps" title="Eurocorps">
        Eurocorps
       </a>
       , as well as the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">
        European Parliament
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Ombudsman" title="European Ombudsman">
        European Ombudsman
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       . The city is also the seat of the
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Commission_for_Navigation_on_the_Rhine" title="Central Commission for Navigation on the Rhine">
        Central Commission for Navigation on the Rhine
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Institute_of_Human_Rights" title="International Institute of Human Rights">
        International Institute of Human Rights
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Strasbourg's historic city centre, the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Grande_%C3%8Ele_(Strasbourg)" title="Grande Île (Strasbourg)">
         Grande Île
        </a>
       </i>
       (Grand Island), was classified a
       <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
        World Heritage site
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
        UNESCO
       </a>
       in 1988, the first time such an honour was placed on an entire city centre. Strasbourg is immersed in the Franco-German culture and although violently disputed throughout history, has been a cultural bridge between France and Germany for centuries, especially through the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Strasbourg" title="University of Strasbourg">
        University of Strasbourg
       </a>
       , currently the second largest in France, and the coexistence of Catholic and
       <a href="/wiki/Protestant_culture" title="Protestant culture">
        Protestant culture
       </a>
       . The largest Islamic place of worship in France, the
       <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg_Mosque" title="Strasbourg Mosque">
        Strasbourg Grand Mosque
       </a>
       , was inaugurated by French Interior Minister Manuel Valls on 27 September 2012.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Economically, Strasbourg is an important centre of manufacturing and engineering, as well as a hub of road, rail, and river transportation. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port_autonome_de_Strasbourg" title="Port autonome de Strasbourg">
        port of Strasbourg
       </a>
       is the second largest on the
       <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">
        Rhine
       </a>
       after
       <a href="/wiki/Duisburg" title="Duisburg">
        Duisburg
       </a>
       , Germany.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_and_names">
        Etymology and names
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology and names">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Before the 5th century, the city was known as
       <i>
        Argantorati
       </i>
       (in the
       <a href="/wiki/Nominative_case" title="Nominative case">
        nominative
       </a>
       ,
       <i>
        Argantorate
       </i>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Locative_case" title="Locative case">
        locative
       </a>
       ), a Celtic
       <a href="/wiki/Gaulish_language" title="Gaulish language">
        Gaulish
       </a>
       name
       <a href="/wiki/Latinisation_of_names" title="Latinisation of names">
        Latinized
       </a>
       first as
       <i>
        Argentorate
       </i>
       (with Gaulish locative ending, as appearing on the first
       <a href="/wiki/Milestone#Roman_Empire" title="Milestone">
        Roman milestones
       </a>
       in the 1st century CE), and then as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Argentoratum" title="Argentoratum">
         Argentoratum
        </a>
       </i>
       (with regular Latin nominative ending, in later Latin texts). That Gaulish name is a compound of
       <i>
        -rati
       </i>
       , the Gaulish word for fortified enclosures, cognate to the
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Irish" title="Old Irish">
        Old Irish
       </a>
       <i>
        ráth
       </i>
       (see
       <a href="/wiki/Ringfort" title="Ringfort">
        ringfort
       </a>
       ), and
       <i>
        arganto(n)-
       </i>
       (cognate to Latin
       <i>
        argentum
       </i>
       , which gave modern French
       <i>
        argent
       </i>
       ), the Gaulish word for silver, but also any precious metal, particularly gold, suggesting either a fortified enclosure located by a river gold mining site, or hoarding gold mined in the nearby rivers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After the 5th century, the city became known by a completely different name
       <a href="/wiki/Francization" title="Francization">
        Gallicized
       </a>
       as Strasbourg (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alsatian_language" title="Alsatian language">
        Lower Alsatian
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        Strossburi
       </i>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Alemannic_German" title="Help:IPA/Alemannic German">
         [ˈʃd̥rɔːsb̥uri]
        </a>
       </span>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
        German
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="de">
         Straßburg
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">
         [ˈʃtʁaːsbʊɐ̯k]
        </a>
       </span>
       ). That name is of
       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">
        Germanic
       </a>
       origin and means "Town (at the crossing) of roads". The modern
       <i>
        Stras-
       </i>
       is
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cognate_(etymology)" title="Cognate (etymology)">
        cognate
       </a>
       to the German
       <i>
        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Stra%C3%9Fe" title="wikt:Straße">
         Straße
        </a>
       </i>
       and English
       <i>
        street
       </i>
       , all of which are derived from
       <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
        Latin
       </a>
       <i>
        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/strata#Latin" title="wikt:strata">
         strata
        </a>
       </i>
       ("paved road"), while
       <i>
        -bourg
       </i>
       is cognate to the German
       <i>
        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Burg" title="wikt:Burg">
         Burg
        </a>
       </i>
       and English
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Borough" title="Borough">
         borough
        </a>
       </i>
       , all of which are derived from
       <a href="/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" title="Proto-Germanic language">
        Proto-Germanic
       </a>
       <i>
        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Appendix:Proto-Germanic/burgz" title="wikt:Appendix:Proto-Germanic/burgz">
         *burgz
        </a>
       </i>
       ("hill fort, fortress").
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Gregory_of_Tours" title="Gregory of Tours">
        Gregory of Tours
       </a>
       was the first to mention the name change: in the tenth book of his
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Gregory_of_Tours#History_of_the_Franks" title="Gregory of Tours">
         History of the Franks
        </a>
       </i>
       written shortly after 590 he said that
       <a href="/wiki/Egidius_(bishop_of_Reims)" title="Egidius (bishop of Reims)">
        Egidius
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Reims" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Reims">
        Bishop of Reims
       </a>
       , accused of plotting against King
       <a href="/wiki/Childebert_II" title="Childebert II">
        Childebert II
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Austrasia" title="Austrasia">
        Austrasia
       </a>
       in favor of his uncle King
       <a href="/wiki/Chilperic_I" title="Chilperic I">
        Chilperic I
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Neustria" title="Neustria">
        Neustria
       </a>
       , was tried by a
       <a href="/wiki/Synod" title="Synod">
        synod
       </a>
       of Austrasian bishops in
       <a href="/wiki/Metz" title="Metz">
        Metz
       </a>
       in November 590, found guilty and removed from the priesthood, then taken "
       <i>
        ad Argentoratensem urbem, quam nunc Strateburgum vocant
       </i>
       " ("to the city of Argentoratum, which they now call
       <i>
        Strateburgus
       </i>
       "), where he was exiled.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Location">
        Location
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Location">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Strasbourg_SPOT_1163.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Strasbourg_SPOT_1163.jpg/220px-Strasbourg_SPOT_1163.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Strasbourg_SPOT_1163.jpg/330px-Strasbourg_SPOT_1163.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Strasbourg_SPOT_1163.jpg/440px-Strasbourg_SPOT_1163.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Strasbourg_SPOT_1163.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Strasbourg seen from Spot Satellite
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Strasbourg is situated on the eastern border of France with Germany. This border is formed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">
        Rhine
       </a>
       , which also forms the eastern border of the modern city, facing across the river to the German town
       <a href="/wiki/Kehl" title="Kehl">
        Kehl
       </a>
       . The historic core of Strasbourg however lies on the
       <a href="/wiki/Grande_%C3%8Ele_(Strasbourg)" title="Grande Île (Strasbourg)">
        Grande Île
       </a>
       in the river
       <a href="/wiki/Ill_(France)" title="Ill (France)">
        Ill
       </a>
       , which here flows parallel to, and roughly 4 kilometres (2.5 mi) from, the Rhine. The natural courses of the two rivers eventually join some distance downstream of Strasbourg, although several artificial waterways now connect them within the city.
      </p>
      <p>
       The city lies in the
       <a href="/wiki/Upper_Rhine_Plain" title="Upper Rhine Plain">
        Upper Rhine Plain
       </a>
       , at between 132 metres (433 ft) and 151 metres (495 ft) above sea level, with the upland areas of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vosges_Mountains" title="Vosges Mountains">
        Vosges Mountains
       </a>
       some 20 km (12 mi) to the west and the
       <a href="/wiki/Black_Forest" title="Black Forest">
        Black Forest
       </a>
       25 km (16 mi) to the east. This section of the Rhine valley is a major axis of north–south travel, with river traffic on the Rhine itself, and major roads and railways paralleling it on both banks.
      </p>
      <p>
       The city is some 400 kilometres (250 mi) east of
       <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">
        Paris
       </a>
       . The mouth of the Rhine lies approximately 450 kilometres (280 mi) to the north, or 650 kilometres (400 mi) as the river flows, whilst the head of navigation in
       <a href="/wiki/Basel" title="Basel">
        Basel
       </a>
       is some 100 kilometres (62 mi) to the south, or 150 kilometres (93 mi) by river.
      </p>
      <div style="clear:left;">
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Climatediagram-metric-english-Strasbourg-France-1961-1990.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="685" data-file-width="1000" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Climatediagram-metric-english-Strasbourg-France-1961-1990.png/220px-Climatediagram-metric-english-Strasbourg-France-1961-1990.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Climatediagram-metric-english-Strasbourg-France-1961-1990.png/330px-Climatediagram-metric-english-Strasbourg-France-1961-1990.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Climatediagram-metric-english-Strasbourg-France-1961-1990.png/440px-Climatediagram-metric-english-Strasbourg-France-1961-1990.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Climatediagram-metric-english-Strasbourg-France-1961-1990.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Climate diagram of Strasbourg
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In spite of its position far inland, Strasbourg's climate is classified as
       <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">
        oceanic
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
        Köppen climate classification
       </a>
       <i>
        Cfb
       </i>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with warm, relatively sunny summers and cool,
       <a href="/wiki/Overcast" title="Overcast">
        overcast
       </a>
       winters. Precipitation is elevated from mid-spring to the end of summer, but remains largely constant throughout the year, totaling 631.4 mm (24.9 in) annually. On average, snow falls 30 days per year.
      </p>
      <p>
       The highest temperature ever recorded was 38.5 °C (101.3 °F) in August 2003, during the
       <a href="/wiki/2003_European_heat_wave" title="2003 European heat wave">
        2003 European heat wave
       </a>
       . The lowest temperature ever recorded was −23.4 °C (−10.1 °F) in December 1938.
      </p>
      <p>
       Strasbourg's location in the Rhine valley, sheltered from the dominant winds by the Vosges and Black Forest mountains, results in poor natural ventilation, making Strasbourg one of the most atmospherically polluted cities of France.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nonetheless, the progressive disappearance of
       <a href="/wiki/Heavy_industry" title="Heavy industry">
        heavy industry
       </a>
       on both banks of the Rhine, as well as effective measures of traffic regulation in and around the city have reduced air pollution.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%; text-align:center; font-size:90%; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="14">
         Climate data for Strasbourg, Bas-Rhin, France (1981–2010 averages)

       </tr>

        </th>

        </th>
        <th scope="col">

        </th>

        </th>

         <br/>
         (63.5)
        </td>
