      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Strasbourg" title="History of Strasbourg">
        History of Strasbourg
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Strasbourg" title="Timeline of Strasbourg">
        Timeline of Strasbourg
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Entr%C3%A9e_solennelle_de_l%27empereur_Sigismond_%C3%A0_Strasbourg_en_1414_(3).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1365" data-file-width="2048" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Entr%C3%A9e_solennelle_de_l%27empereur_Sigismond_%C3%A0_Strasbourg_en_1414_%283%29.jpg/220px-Entr%C3%A9e_solennelle_de_l%27empereur_Sigismond_%C3%A0_Strasbourg_en_1414_%283%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Entr%C3%A9e_solennelle_de_l%27empereur_Sigismond_%C3%A0_Strasbourg_en_1414_%283%29.jpg/330px-Entr%C3%A9e_solennelle_de_l%27empereur_Sigismond_%C3%A0_Strasbourg_en_1414_%283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Entr%C3%A9e_solennelle_de_l%27empereur_Sigismond_%C3%A0_Strasbourg_en_1414_%283%29.jpg/440px-Entr%C3%A9e_solennelle_de_l%27empereur_Sigismond_%C3%A0_Strasbourg_en_1414_%283%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Entr%C3%A9e_solennelle_de_l%27empereur_Sigismond_%C3%A0_Strasbourg_en_1414_(3).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Sigismund,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Sigismund, Holy Roman Emperor">
          Sigismund, Holy Roman Emperor
         </a>
         visiting Strasbourg in 1414, detail of a painting by
         <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9o_Schnug" title="Léo Schnug">
          Léo Schnug
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Castra" title="Castra">
        Roman camp
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Argentoratum" title="Argentoratum">
        Argentoratum
       </a>
       was first mentioned in 12 BC; the city of Strasbourg which grew from it celebrated its 2,000th anniversary in 1988. The fertile area between the rivers
       <a href="/wiki/Ill_(France)" title="Ill (France)">
        Ill
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">
        Rhine
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Ried" title="Grand Ried">
        Grand Ried
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Petit_Ried" title="Petit Ried">
        Petit Ried
       </a>
       ) had already been populated since the middle
       <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">
        Paleolithic
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Between 362 and 1262, Strasbourg was governed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Strasbourg" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Strasbourg">
        bishops of Strasbourg
       </a>
       ; their rule was reinforced in 873 and then more in 982.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1262, the citizens violently rebelled against the bishop's rule (
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hausbergen" title="Battle of Hausbergen">
        Battle of Hausbergen
       </a>
       ) and Strasbourg became a
       <a href="/wiki/Free_imperial_city" title="Free imperial city">
        free imperial city
       </a>
       . It became a French city in 1681, after the conquest of Alsace by the armies of
       <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV_of_France" title="Louis XIV of France">
        Louis XIV
       </a>
       . In 1871, after the
       <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_War" title="Franco-Prussian War">
        Franco-Prussian War
       </a>
       , the city became German again, until 1918 (end of
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
       ), when it reverted to France. After the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_France" title="Battle of France">
        defeat of France
       </a>
       in 1940 (
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       ), Strasbourg came under German control again; since the end of 1944, it is again a French town. In 2016, Strasbourg was promoted from capital of
       <a href="/wiki/Alsace" title="Alsace">
        Alsace
       </a>
       to capital of
       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Est" title="Grand Est">
        Grand Est
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Strasbourg played an important part in
       <a href="/wiki/Reformation" title="Reformation">
        Protestant Reformation
       </a>
       , with personalities such as
       <a href="/wiki/John_Calvin" title="John Calvin">
        John Calvin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Martin_Bucer" title="Martin Bucer">
        Martin Bucer
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Capito" title="Wolfgang Capito">
        Wolfgang Capito
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Katharina_Zell" title="Katharina Zell">
        Katharina Zell
       </a>
       , but also in other aspects of Christianity such as
       <a href="/wiki/German_mysticism" title="German mysticism">
        German mysticism
       </a>
       , with
       <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Tauler" title="Johannes Tauler">
        Johannes Tauler
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pietism" title="Pietism">
        Pietism
       </a>
       , with
       <a href="/wiki/Philipp_Spener" title="Philipp Spener">
        Philipp Spener
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Reverence_for_Life" title="Reverence for Life">
        Reverence for Life
       </a>
       , with
       <a href="/wiki/Albert_Schweitzer" title="Albert Schweitzer">
        Albert Schweitzer
       </a>
       . Delegates from the city took part in the
       <a href="/wiki/Protestation_at_Speyer" title="Protestation at Speyer">
        Protestation at Speyer
       </a>
       . It was also one of the first centres of the printing industry with pioneers such as
       <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Gutenberg" title="Johannes Gutenberg">
        Johannes Gutenberg
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Mentelin" title="Johannes Mentelin">
        Johannes Mentelin
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Eggestein" title="Heinrich Eggestein">
        Heinrich Eggestein
       </a>
       . Among the darkest periods in the city's long history were the years 1349 (
       <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg_massacre" title="Strasbourg massacre">
        Strasbourg massacre
       </a>
       ), 1793 (
       <a href="/wiki/Reign_of_Terror" title="Reign of Terror">
        Reign of Terror
       </a>
       ), 1870 (
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Strasbourg" title="Siege of Strasbourg">
        Siege of Strasbourg
       </a>
       ) and the years 1940–1944 with the Nazi occupation (atrocities such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Jewish_skeleton_collection" title="Jewish skeleton collection">
        Jewish skeleton collection
       </a>
       ) and the British and American
       <a href="/wiki/Strategic_bombing_during_World_War_II" title="Strategic bombing during World War II">
        bombing raids
       </a>
       . Some other notable dates were the years 357 (
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Strasbourg" title="Battle of Strasbourg">
        Battle of Argentoratum
       </a>
       ), 842 (
       <a href="/wiki/Oaths_of_Strasbourg" title="Oaths of Strasbourg">
        Oaths of Strasbourg
       </a>
       ), 1538 (establishment of
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Strasbourg" title="University of Strasbourg">
        the university
       </a>
       ), 1605 (world's first newspaper printed by
       <a href="/wiki/Johann_Carolus" title="Johann Carolus">
        Johann Carolus
       </a>
       ), 1792 (
       <a href="/wiki/La_Marseillaise" title="La Marseillaise">
        La Marseillaise
       </a>
       ), and 1889 (pancreatic origin of
       <a href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus" title="Diabetes mellitus">
        diabetes
       </a>
       discovered by
       <a href="/wiki/Oskar_Minkowski" title="Oskar Minkowski">
        Minkowski
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_von_Mering" title="Joseph von Mering">
        Von Mering
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       Strasbourg is the seat of
       <a href="/wiki/European_institutions_in_Strasbourg" title="European institutions in Strasbourg">
        European Institutions
       </a>
       since 1949: first of the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Commission_on_Civil_Status" title="International Commission on Civil Status">
        International Commission on Civil Status
       </a>
       and of the
       <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">
        Council of Europe
       </a>
       , later of the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">
        European Parliament
       </a>
       , of the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Science_Foundation" title="European Science Foundation">
        European Science Foundation
       </a>
       , of
       <a href="/wiki/Eurocorps" title="Eurocorps">
        Eurocorps
       </a>
       , and others as well.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Districts">
        Districts
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Districts">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Strasbourg is divided into the following districts:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        Bourse, Esplanade, Krutenau
       </li>
       <li>
        Centre République
       </li>
       <li>
        Centre Gare
       </li>
       <li>
        Conseil des XV, Rotterdam
       </li>
       <li>
        Cronenbourg, Hautepierre, Poteries, Hohberg
       </li>
       <li>
        Koenigshoffen, Montagne-Verte, Elsau
       </li>
       <li>
        Meinau
       </li>
       <li>
        Neudorf, Schluthfeld, Port du Rhin, Musau
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Neuhof,_Strasbourg" title="Neuhof, Strasbourg">
         Neuhof, Stockfeld, Ganzau
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Robertsau, Wacken
       </li>
      </ol>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Main_sights">
        Main sights
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Main sights">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:767px;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Strasbourg_-_Ponts_Couverts_vus_de_la_terrasse_panoramique.jpg">
          <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="3104" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Strasbourg_-_Ponts_Couverts_vus_de_la_terrasse_panoramique.jpg/765px-Strasbourg_-_Ponts_Couverts_vus_de_la_terrasse_panoramique.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Strasbourg_-_Ponts_Couverts_vus_de_la_terrasse_panoramique.jpg/1148px-Strasbourg_-_Ponts_Couverts_vus_de_la_terrasse_panoramique.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Strasbourg_-_Ponts_Couverts_vus_de_la_terrasse_panoramique.jpg/1530px-Strasbourg_-_Ponts_Couverts_vus_de_la_terrasse_panoramique.jpg 2x" width="765"/>
         </a>
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Strasbourg_-_Ponts_Couverts_vus_de_la_terrasse_panoramique.jpg" title="Enlarge">
           </a>
          </div>
          Panorama from the
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Barrage_Vauban" title="Barrage Vauban">
            Barrage Vauban
           </a>
          </i>
          with the medieval bridge
          <i>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ponts_Couverts_(Strasbourg)" title="Ponts Couverts (Strasbourg)">
            Ponts Couverts
           </a>
          </i>
          in the foreground (the fourth tower being hidden by trees at the left) and the
          <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg_Cathedral" title="Strasbourg Cathedral">
           cathedral
          </a>
          in the distance on the right.
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">
        Architecture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Architecture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Strasbourg_Cathedral_Exterior_-_Diliff.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="8402" data-file-width="6574" height="281" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Strasbourg_Cathedral_Exterior_-_Diliff.jpg/220px-Strasbourg_Cathedral_Exterior_-_Diliff.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Strasbourg_Cathedral_Exterior_-_Diliff.jpg/330px-Strasbourg_Cathedral_Exterior_-_Diliff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Strasbourg_Cathedral_Exterior_-_Diliff.jpg/440px-Strasbourg_Cathedral_Exterior_-_Diliff.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Strasbourg_Cathedral_Exterior_-_Diliff.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg_Cathedral" title="Strasbourg Cathedral">
          Strasbourg, Cathedral of Our Lady
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The city is chiefly known for its
       <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">
        sandstone
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">
        Gothic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg_Cathedral" title="Strasbourg Cathedral">
        Cathedral
       </a>
       with its famous
       <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg_astronomical_clock" title="Strasbourg astronomical clock">
        astronomical clock
       </a>
       , and for its medieval cityscape of
       <a href="/wiki/Rhineland" title="Rhineland">
        Rhineland
       </a>
       black and white
       <a href="/wiki/Timber_framing" title="Timber framing">
        timber-framed
       </a>
       buildings, particularly in the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Petite_France,_Strasbourg" title="Petite France, Strasbourg">
         Petite France
        </a>
       </i>
       district or
       <i>
        Gerberviertel
       </i>
       ("tanners' district") alongside the Ill and in the streets and squares surrounding the cathedral, where the renowned
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Kammerzell_House" title="Kammerzell House">
         Maison Kammerzell
        </a>
       </i>
       stands out.
      </p>
      <p>
       Notable medieval streets include
       <i>
        Rue Mercière
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Rue des Dentelles
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Rue du Bain aux Plantes
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Rue des Juifs
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Rue des Frères
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Rue des Tonneliers
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Rue du Maroquin
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Rue des Charpentiers
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Rue des Serruriers
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Grand' Rue
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Quai des Bateliers
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Quai Saint-Nicolas
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Quai Saint-Thomas
       </i>
       . Notable medieval squares include
       <i>
        Place de la Cathédrale
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Place du Marché Gayot
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Place Saint-Étienne
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Place du Marché aux Cochons de Lait
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Place Benjamin Zix
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Absolute_Pl_marche_aux_cochons_01.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Absolute_Pl_marche_aux_cochons_01.JPG/220px-Absolute_Pl_marche_aux_cochons_01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Absolute_Pl_marche_aux_cochons_01.JPG/330px-Absolute_Pl_marche_aux_cochons_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Absolute_Pl_marche_aux_cochons_01.JPG/440px-Absolute_Pl_marche_aux_cochons_01.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Absolute_Pl_marche_aux_cochons_01.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          Place du Marché aux Cochons de Lait
         </i>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Strasbourg_place_gutenberg.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2417" data-file-width="4113" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Strasbourg_place_gutenberg.jpg/220px-Strasbourg_place_gutenberg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Strasbourg_place_gutenberg.jpg/330px-Strasbourg_place_gutenberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Strasbourg_place_gutenberg.jpg/440px-Strasbourg_place_gutenberg.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Strasbourg_place_gutenberg.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Place Gutenberg with statue of Gutenberg and Carousel.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Absolute_Maison_des_tanneurs_01.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Absolute_Maison_des_tanneurs_01.JPG/220px-Absolute_Maison_des_tanneurs_01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Absolute_Maison_des_tanneurs_01.JPG/330px-Absolute_Maison_des_tanneurs_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Absolute_Maison_des_tanneurs_01.JPG/440px-Absolute_Maison_des_tanneurs_01.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Absolute_Maison_des_tanneurs_01.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          Maison des tanneurs
         </i>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Strasbourgriver.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2304" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Strasbourgriver.jpg/220px-Strasbourgriver.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Strasbourgriver.jpg/330px-Strasbourgriver.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Strasbourgriver.jpg/440px-Strasbourgriver.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Strasbourgriver.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         View of the Ill with
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Thomas,_Strasbourg" title="St. Thomas, Strasbourg">
          Église Saint-Thomas
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In addition to the cathedral, Strasbourg houses several other medieval churches that have survived the many wars and destructions that have plagued the city: the
       <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">
        Romanesque
       </a>
       <i>
        Église Saint-Étienne
       </i>
       , partly destroyed in 1944 by Allied
       <a href="/wiki/Strategic_bombing" title="Strategic bombing">
        bombing raids
       </a>
       , the part Romanesque, part Gothic, very large
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Thomas,_Strasbourg" title="St. Thomas, Strasbourg">
         Église Saint-Thomas
        </a>
       </i>
       with its
       <a href="/wiki/Gottfried_Silbermann" title="Gottfried Silbermann">
        Silbermann
       </a>
       organ on which
       <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">
        Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Albert_Schweitzer" title="Albert Schweitzer">
        Albert Schweitzer
       </a>
       played,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the Gothic
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Saint-Pierre-le-Jeune_Protestant_Church" title="Saint-Pierre-le-Jeune Protestant Church">
         Église protestante Saint-Pierre-le-Jeune
        </a>
       </i>
       with its crypt dating back to the seventh century and its
       <a href="/wiki/Cloister" title="Cloister">
        cloister
       </a>
       partly from the eleventh century, the Gothic
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_William%27s_Church,_Strasbourg" title="Saint William's Church, Strasbourg">
         Église Saint-Guillaume
        </a>
       </i>
       with its fine early-Renaissance
       <a href="/wiki/Stained_glass" title="Stained glass">
        stained glass
       </a>
       and furniture, the Gothic
       <i>
        Église Saint-Jean
       </i>
       , the part Gothic, part
       <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">
        Art Nouveau
       </a>
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sainte-Madeleine_Church,_Strasbourg" title="Sainte-Madeleine Church, Strasbourg">
         Église Sainte-Madeleine
        </a>
       </i>
       , etc. The
       <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">
        Neo-Gothic
       </a>
       church
       <i>
        Saint-Pierre-le-Vieux Catholique
       </i>
       (there is also an adjacent church
       <i>
        Saint-Pierre-le-Vieux Protestant
       </i>
       ) serves as a shrine for several 15th-century wood worked and painted
       <a href="/wiki/Altar#In_Western_Christian_churches" title="Altar">
        altars
       </a>
       coming from other, now destroyed churches and installed there for public display. Among the numerous secular medieval buildings, the monumental
       <i>
        Ancienne Douane
       </i>
       (old
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Custom_House" title="Custom House">
        custom-house
       </a>
       ) stands out.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/German_Renaissance" title="German Renaissance">
        German Renaissance
       </a>
       has bequeathed the city some noteworthy buildings (especially
       <a href="/wiki/Neubau_(Strasbourg)" title="Neubau (Strasbourg)">
        the current
        <i>
         Chambre de commerce et d'industrie
        </i>
       </a>
       , former
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_and_town_halls" title="City and town halls">
        town hall
       </a>
       , on
       <i>
        Place Gutenberg
       </i>
       ), as did the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Baroque_and_Classicism" title="French Baroque and Classicism">
        French Baroque and Classicism
       </a>
       with several
       <i>
        hôtels particuliers
       </i>
       (i.e.
       <a href="/wiki/Palace" title="Palace">
        palaces
       </a>
       ), among which the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Palais_Rohan,_Strasbourg" title="Palais Rohan, Strasbourg">
         Palais Rohan
        </a>
       </i>
       (1742, now housing three museums) is the most spectacular. Other buildings of its kind are the "
       <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B4tel_de_Hanau" title="Hôtel de Hanau">
        Hôtel de Hanau
       </a>
       " (1736, now the city hall), the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B4tel_de_Klinglin" title="Hôtel de Klinglin">
         Hôtel de Klinglin
        </a>
       </i>
       (1736, now residence of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pr%C3%A9fet" title="Préfet">
        préfet
       </a>
       ), the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B4tel_des_Deux-Ponts" title="Hôtel des Deux-Ponts">
         Hôtel des Deux-Ponts
        </a>
       </i>
       (1755, now residence of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_Governor" title="Military Governor">
        military governor
       </a>
       ), the
       <i>
        Hôtel d'Andlau-Klinglin
       </i>
       (1725, now seat of the administration of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port_autonome_de_Strasbourg" title="Port autonome de Strasbourg">
        Port autonome de Strasbourg
       </a>
       ) etc. The largest baroque building of Strasbourg though is the 150-metre-long (490 ft) 1720s main building of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B4pital_civil,_Strasbourg" title="Hôpital civil, Strasbourg">
         Hôpital civil
        </a>
       </i>
       . As for French
       <a href="/wiki/Neoclassicism" title="Neoclassicism">
        Neo-classicism
       </a>
       , it is the
       <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg_Opera_House" title="Strasbourg Opera House">
        Opera House
       </a>
       on
       <a href="/wiki/Place_Broglie" title="Place Broglie">
        Place Broglie
       </a>
       that most prestigiously represents this style.
      </p>
      <p>
       Strasbourg also offers high-class
       <a href="/wiki/Eclecticism_in_art" title="Eclecticism in art">
        eclecticist
       </a>
       buildings in its very extended German district, the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Neustadt_(Strasbourg)" title="Neustadt (Strasbourg)">
         Neustadt
        </a>
       </i>
       , being the main memory of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wilhelm_I,_German_Emperor" title="Wilhelm I, German Emperor">
        Wilhelmian architecture
       </a>
       since most of the major cities in Germany proper suffered intensive damage during World War II. Streets, boulevards and avenues are homogeneous, surprisingly high (up to seven stories) and broad examples of German urban lay-out and of this
       <a href="/wiki/Architectural_style" title="Architectural style">
        architectural style
       </a>
       that summons and mixes up five centuries of European architecture as well as Neo-Egyptian,
       <a href="/wiki/Neo-Grec" title="Neo-Grec">
        Neo-Greek
       </a>
       and Neo-Babylonian styles. The former imperial palace
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Palais_du_Rhin" title="Palais du Rhin">
         Palais du Rhin
        </a>
       </i>
       , the most political and thus heavily criticized of all German Strasbourg buildings epitomizes the grand scale and stylistic sturdiness of this period. But the two most handsome and ornate buildings of these times are the
       <i>
        École internationale des Pontonniers
       </i>
       (the former
       <i>
        Höhere Mädchenschule
       </i>
       , girls college) with its towers, turrets and multiple round and square angles
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Haute_%C3%A9cole_des_arts_du_Rhin" title="Haute école des arts du Rhin">
         Haute école des arts du Rhin
        </a>
       </i>
       with its lavishly ornate façade of painted bricks, woodwork and
       <a href="/wiki/Maiolica" title="Maiolica">
        majolica
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:OrgueSaintThomasStrasbourg.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/OrgueSaintThomasStrasbourg.jpg/220px-OrgueSaintThomasStrasbourg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/OrgueSaintThomasStrasbourg.jpg/330px-OrgueSaintThomasStrasbourg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/OrgueSaintThomasStrasbourg.jpg/440px-OrgueSaintThomasStrasbourg.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:OrgueSaintThomasStrasbourg.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The baroque organ of the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Thomas,_Strasbourg" title="St. Thomas, Strasbourg">
          Église Saint-Thomas
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Notable streets of the German district include:
       <i>
        Avenue de la Forêt Noire
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Avenue des Vosges
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Avenue d'Alsace
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Avenue de la Marseillaise
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Avenue de la Liberté
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Boulevard de la Victoire
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Rue Sellénick
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Rue du Général de Castelnau
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Rue du Maréchal Foch
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        Rue du Maréchal Joffre
       </i>
       . Notable squares of the German district include:
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Place_de_la_R%C3%A9publique_(Strasbourg)" title="Place de la République (Strasbourg)">
         Place de la République
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Place de l'Université
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Place Brant
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        Place Arnold
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Impressive examples of
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">
        Prussian
       </a>
       military architecture of the 1880s can be found along the newly reopened
       <i>
        Rue du Rempart
       </i>
       , displaying large-scale fortifications among which the aptly named
       <i>
        Kriegstor
       </i>
       (war gate).
      </p>
      <p>
       As for modern and
       <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_architecture" title="Contemporary architecture">
        contemporary architecture
       </a>
       , Strasbourg possesses some fine
       <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">
        Art Nouveau
       </a>
       buildings (such as the huge
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Palais_des_F%C3%AAtes" title="Palais des Fêtes">
         Palais des Fêtes
        </a>
       </i>
       and houses and villas like
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Villa_Schutzenberger" title="Villa Schutzenberger">
         Villa Schutzenberger
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B4tel_Brion" title="Hôtel Brion">
         Hôtel Brion
        </a>
       </i>
       ), good examples of post-World War II functional architecture (the
       <i>
        Cité Rotterdam
       </i>
       , for which
       <a href="/wiki/Le_Corbusier" title="Le Corbusier">
        Le Corbusier
       </a>
       did not succeed in the architectural contest) and, in the very extended
       <i>
        Quartier Européen
       </i>
       , some spectacular administrative buildings of sometimes utterly large size, among which the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Human_Rights_building" title="European Court of Human Rights building">
        European Court of Human Rights building
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Rogers" title="Richard Rogers">
        Richard Rogers
       </a>
       is arguably the finest. Other noticeable contemporary buildings are the new
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/College_or_university_school_of_music" title="College or university school of music">
        Music school
       </a>
       <i>
        Cité de la Musique et de la Danse
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg_Museum_of_Modern_and_Contemporary_Art" title="Strasbourg Museum of Modern and Contemporary Art">
         Musée d'Art moderne et contemporain
        </a>
       </i>
       and the
       <i>
        Hôtel du Département
       </i>
       facing it, as well as, in the outskirts, the tramway-station
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hoenheim" title="Hoenheim">
        Hoenheim
       </a>
       -Nord designed by
       <a href="/wiki/Zaha_Hadid" title="Zaha Hadid">
        Zaha Hadid
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Absolute_place_Kleber_02.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1587" data-file-width="2559" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Absolute_place_Kleber_02.jpg/220px-Absolute_place_Kleber_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Absolute_place_Kleber_02.jpg/330px-Absolute_place_Kleber_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Absolute_place_Kleber_02.jpg/440px-Absolute_place_Kleber_02.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Absolute_place_Kleber_02.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Place_Kl%C3%A9ber" title="Place Kléber">
           Place Kléber
          </a>
         </i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The city has many bridges, including the medieval and four-towered
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ponts_Couverts_(Strasbourg)" title="Ponts Couverts (Strasbourg)">
         Ponts Couverts
        </a>
       </i>
       that, despite their name, are no longer covered. Next to the
       <i>
        Ponts Couverts
       </i>
       is the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Barrage_Vauban" title="Barrage Vauban">
         Barrage Vauban
        </a>
       </i>
       , a part of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vauban" title="Vauban">
        Vauban
       </a>
       's 17th-century fortifications, that does include a covered bridge. Other bridges are the ornate 19th-century
       <i>
        Pont de la Fonderie
       </i>
       (1893, stone) and
       <i>
        Pont d'Auvergne
       </i>
       (1892, iron), as well as architect
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Marc_Mimram&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Marc Mimram (page does not exist)">
        Marc Mimram
       </a>
       's futuristic
       <i>
        Passerelle
       </i>
       over the Rhine, opened in 2004.
      </p>
      <p>
       The largest square at the centre of the city of Strasbourg is the
       <a href="/wiki/Place_Kl%C3%A9ber" title="Place Kléber">
        Place Kléber
       </a>
       . Located in the heart of the city's commercial area, it was named after general
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jean_Baptiste_Kl%C3%A9ber" title="Jean Baptiste Kléber">
        Jean-Baptiste Kléber
       </a>
       , born in Strasbourg in 1753 and assassinated in 1800 in
       <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">
        Cairo
       </a>
       . In the square is a statue of Kléber, under which is a vault containing his remains. On the north side of the square is the
       <a href="/wiki/Aubette_(building)" title="Aubette (building)">
        Aubette
       </a>
       (Orderly Room), built by
       <a href="/wiki/Jacques-Fran%C3%A7ois_Blondel" title="Jacques-François Blondel">
        Jacques François Blondel
       </a>
       , architect of the king, in 1765–1772.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Parks">
        Parks
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Parks">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Absolute_Pavillon_Jos%C3%A9phine_01.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Absolute_Pavillon_Jos%C3%A9phine_01.jpg/220px-Absolute_Pavillon_Jos%C3%A9phine_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Absolute_Pavillon_Jos%C3%A9phine_01.jpg/330px-Absolute_Pavillon_Jos%C3%A9phine_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Absolute_Pavillon_Jos%C3%A9phine_01.jpg/440px-Absolute_Pavillon_Jos%C3%A9phine_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Absolute_Pavillon_Jos%C3%A9phine_01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <i>
          Pavillon Joséphine
         </i>
         (rear side) in the
         <i>
          Parc de l'Orangerie
         </i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Absolute_Chateau_de_Pourtales_01.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Absolute_Chateau_de_Pourtales_01.JPG/220px-Absolute_Chateau_de_Pourtales_01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Absolute_Chateau_de_Pourtales_01.JPG/330px-Absolute_Chateau_de_Pourtales_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Absolute_Chateau_de_Pourtales_01.JPG/440px-Absolute_Chateau_de_Pourtales_01.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Absolute_Chateau_de_Pourtales_01.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <i>
          Château de Pourtalès
         </i>
         (front side) in the park of the same name
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Strasbourg features a number of prominent parks, of which several are of cultural and historical interest: the
       <i>
        Parc de l'Orangerie
       </i>
       , laid out as a French garden by
       <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Le_N%C3%B4tre" title="André Le Nôtre">
        André le Nôtre
       </a>
       and remodeled as an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landscape_garden" title="Landscape garden">
        English garden
       </a>
       on behalf of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9phine_de_Beauharnais" title="Joséphine de Beauharnais">
        Joséphine de Beauharnais
       </a>
       , now displaying noteworthy French gardens, a neo-classical castle and a small
       <a href="/wiki/Zoo" title="Zoo">
        zoo
       </a>
       ; the
       <i>
        Parc de la Citadelle
       </i>
       , built around impressive remains of the 17th-century
       <a href="/wiki/Fortification" title="Fortification">
        fortress
       </a>
       erected close to the
       <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">
        Rhine
       </a>
       by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vauban" title="Vauban">
        Vauban
       </a>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the
       <i>
        Parc de Pourtalès
       </i>
       , laid out in English style around a
       <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">
        baroque
       </a>
       castle (heavily restored in the 19th century) that now houses a small three-star hotel,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and featuring an
       <a href="/wiki/Open-air_museum" title="Open-air museum">
        open-air museum
       </a>
       of international contemporary sculpture.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Jardin_botanique_de_l%27Universit%C3%A9_de_Strasbourg" title="Jardin botanique de l'Université de Strasbourg">
        Jardin botanique de l'Université de Strasbourg
       </a>
       (botanical garden) was created under the German administration next to the
       <a href="/wiki/Observatory_of_Strasbourg" title="Observatory of Strasbourg">
        Observatory of Strasbourg
       </a>
       , built in 1881, and still owns some
       <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse" title="Greenhouse">
        greenhouses
       </a>
       of those times. The
       <i>
        Parc des Contades
       </i>
       , although the oldest park of the city, was completely remodeled after World War II. The futuristic
       <i>
        Parc des Poteries
       </i>
       is an example of European park-conception in the late 1990s. The
       <i>
        Jardin des deux Rives
       </i>
       , spread over Strasbourg and
       <a href="/wiki/Kehl" title="Kehl">
        Kehl
       </a>
       on both sides of the Rhine opened in 2004 and is the most extended (60-hectare) park of the agglomeration. The most recent park is
       <i>
        Parc du Heyritz
       </i>
       (8,7 ha), opened in 2014 along a canal facing the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B4pital_civil,_Strasbourg" title="Hôpital civil, Strasbourg">
         hôpital civil
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">
        Museums
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Museums">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       For a city of comparatively small size, Strasbourg displays a large quantity and variety of museums:
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fine_art_museums">
        Fine art museums
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Fine art museums">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paul_Hannong_Strassburg.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1606" data-file-width="1836" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Paul_Hannong_Strassburg.jpg/220px-Paul_Hannong_Strassburg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Paul_Hannong_Strassburg.jpg/330px-Paul_Hannong_Strassburg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Paul_Hannong_Strassburg.jpg/440px-Paul_Hannong_Strassburg.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paul_Hannong_Strassburg.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A room in the
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_des_Arts_d%C3%A9coratifs,_Strasbourg" title="Musée des Arts décoratifs, Strasbourg">
           Musée des Arts décoratifs
          </a>
         </i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Unlike most other cities, Strasbourg's collections of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_art_history" title="Western art history">
        European art
       </a>
       are divided into several museums according not only to type and area, but also to epoch.
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Master" title="Old Master">
        Old master
       </a>
       paintings from the Germanic
       <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">
        Rhenish
       </a>
       territories and until 1681 are displayed in the
       <i>
        Musée de l'Œuvre Notre-Dame
       </i>
       , old master paintings from all the rest of Europe (including the Dutch Rhenish territories) and until 1871 as well as old master paintings from the Germanic Rhenish territories between 1681 and 1871 are displayed in the
       <i>
        Musée des Beaux-Arts
       </i>
       . Old master
       <a href="/wiki/Graphic_arts" title="Graphic arts">
        graphic arts
       </a>
       until 1871 is displayed in the
       <i>
        Cabinet des estampes et dessins
       </i>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Decorative_arts" title="Decorative arts">
        Decorative arts
       </a>
       until 1681 ("German period") are displayed in the
       <i>
        Musée de l'Œuvre Notre-Dame
       </i>
       , decorative arts from 1681 to 1871 ("French period") are displayed in the
       <i>
        Musée des Arts décoratifs
       </i>
       . International art (painting, sculpture, graphic arts) and decorative art since 1871 is displayed in the
       <i>
        Musée d'art moderne et contemporain
       </i>
       . The latter museum also displays the city's photographic library.
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_des_Beaux-Arts_de_Strasbourg" title="Musée des Beaux-Arts de Strasbourg">
          Musée des Beaux-Arts
         </a>
        </i>
        owns paintings by
        <a href="/wiki/Hans_Memling" title="Hans Memling">
         Hans Memling
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Goya" title="Francisco Goya">
         Francisco de Goya
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Tintoretto" title="Tintoretto">
         Tintoretto
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Veronese" title="Paolo Veronese">
         Paolo Veronese
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Giotto_di_Bondone" title="Giotto di Bondone">
         Giotto di Bondone
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Sandro_Botticelli" title="Sandro Botticelli">
         Sandro Botticelli
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Peter_Paul_Rubens" title="Peter Paul Rubens">
         Peter Paul Rubens
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Anthony_van_Dyck" title="Anthony van Dyck">
         Anthony van Dyck
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/El_Greco" title="El Greco">
         El Greco
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Antonio_da_Correggio" title="Antonio da Correggio">
         Correggio
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Cima_da_Conegliano" title="Cima da Conegliano">
         Cima da Conegliano
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Piero_di_Cosimo" title="Piero di Cosimo">
         Piero di Cosimo
        </a>
        , among others.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_de_l%27%C5%92uvre_Notre-Dame" title="Musée de l'Œuvre Notre-Dame">
          Musée de l'Œuvre Notre-Dame
         </a>
        </i>
        (located in a part-Gothic, part-Renaissance building next to the Cathedral) houses a large and renowned collection of medieval and Renaissance upper-Rhenish art, among which original sculptures, plans and stained glass from the Cathedral and paintings by
        <a href="/wiki/Hans_Baldung" title="Hans Baldung">
         Hans Baldung
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Stoskopff" title="Sebastian Stoskopff">
         Sebastian Stoskopff
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg_Museum_of_Modern_and_Contemporary_Art" title="Strasbourg Museum of Modern and Contemporary Art">
          Musée d'Art moderne et contemporain
         </a>
        </i>
        is among the largest museums of its kind in France.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_des_Arts_d%C3%A9coratifs,_Strasbourg" title="Musée des Arts décoratifs, Strasbourg">
          Musée des Arts décoratifs
         </a>
        </i>
        , located in the sumptuous former residence of the cardinals of Rohan, the
        <a href="/wiki/Palais_Rohan,_Strasbourg" title="Palais Rohan, Strasbourg">
         Palais Rohan
        </a>
        displays a reputable collection of 18th century furniture and china.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cabinet_des_estampes_et_des_dessins_(Strasbourg)" title="Cabinet des estampes et des dessins (Strasbourg)">
          Cabinet des estampes et des dessins
         </a>
        </i>
        displays five centuries of
        <a href="/wiki/Engraving" title="Engraving">
         engravings
        </a>
        and drawings, but also
        <a href="/wiki/Woodcut" title="Woodcut">
         woodcuts
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Lithography" title="Lithography">
         lithographies
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_Tomi_Ungerer/Centre_international_de_l%27illustration" title="Musée Tomi Ungerer/Centre international de l'illustration">
          Musée Tomi Ungerer/Centre international de l'illustration
         </a>
        </i>
        , located in a large former villa next to the Theatre, displays original works by Ungerer and other artists (
        <a href="/wiki/Saul_Steinberg" title="Saul Steinberg">
         Saul Steinberg
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Searle" title="Ronald Searle">
         Ronald Searle
        </a>
        ...) as well as Ungerer's large collection of ancient toys.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_museums">
        Other museums
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Other museums">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_arch%C3%A9ologique_(Strasbourg)" title="Musée archéologique (Strasbourg)">
          Musée archéologique
         </a>
        </i>
        presents a large display of regional findings from the first ages of man to the sixth century, focussing especially on the Roman and Celtic period.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_alsacien_(Strasbourg)" title="Musée alsacien (Strasbourg)">
          Musée alsacien
         </a>
        </i>
        is dedicated to traditional Alsatian daily life.
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Le_Vaisseau" title="Le Vaisseau">
          Le Vaisseau
         </a>
        </i>
        ("The vessel") is a science and technology centre, especially designed for children.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_historique_de_Strasbourg" title="Musée historique de Strasbourg">
          Musée historique
         </a>
        </i>
        (historical museum) is dedicated to the tumultuous history of the city and displays many artifacts of the times, among which the 'Grüselhorn
        <i>
         , the horn that was blown every evening at 10:00, during medieval times, to order the Jews out of the city.
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         Musée de la Navigation sur le Rhin
        </i>
        , also going by the name of
        <i>
         Naviscope
        </i>
        , located in an old ship, is dedicated to the history of commercial navigation on the
        <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">
         Rhine
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         Musée vodou
        </i>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Vodou" title="Haitian Vodou">
         Vodou
        </a>
        museum) opened its doors on 28 November 2013. Displaying a private collection of artefacts from
        <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">
         Haiti
        </a>
        , it is located in a former water tower (
        <i>
         château d'eau
        </i>
        ) built in 1883 and classified as a
        <a href="/wiki/Monument_historique" title="Monument historique">
         Monument historique
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         Musée du barreau de Strasbourg
        </i>
        (The Strasbourg
        <a href="/wiki/Bar_association" title="Bar association">
         bar association
        </a>
        museum) is a museum dedicated to the work and the history of
        <a href="/wiki/Lawyer" title="Lawyer">
         lawyers
        </a>
        in the city.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
         <a href="#cite_note-28">
          [28]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
         <a href="#cite_note-29">
          [29]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="University_museums">
        University museums
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: University museums">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Strasbourg" title="University of Strasbourg">
        Université de Strasbourg
       </a>
       is in charge of a number of permanent public displays of its collections of scientific artefacts and products of all kinds of exploration and research.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_zoologique_de_la_ville_de_Strasbourg" title="Musée zoologique de la ville de Strasbourg">
         <i>
          Musée zoologique
         </i>
        </a>
        is one of the oldest in France and is especially famous for its collection of birds. The museum is co-administrated by the municipality.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Palais_Universitaire,_Strasbourg#Gypsothèque" title="Palais Universitaire, Strasbourg">
         <i>
          Gypsothèque
         </i>
        </a>
        (also known as
        <i>
         Musée des moulages
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         Musée
         <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Michaelis" title="Adolf Michaelis">
          Adolf Michaelis
         </a>
        </i>
        ) is France's second largest
        <a href="/wiki/Plaster_cast" title="Plaster cast">
         cast collection
        </a>
        and the largest university cast collection in France.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         Musée de
         <a href="/wiki/Seismology" title="Seismology">
          Sismologie
         </a>
         et
         <a href="/wiki/Magnetism" title="Magnetism">
          Magnétisme terrestre
         </a>
        </i>
        displays antique instruments of measure
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         Musée
         <a href="/wiki/Louis_Pasteur" title="Louis Pasteur">
          Pasteur
         </a>
        </i>
        is a collection of medical curiosities
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_de_min%C3%A9ralogie" title="Musée de minéralogie">
          Musée de minéralogie
         </a>
        </i>
        is dedicated to minerals
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         Musée d'
         <a href="/wiki/Egyptology" title="Egyptology">
          Égyptologie
         </a>
        </i>
        houses a collections of archaeological findings made in and brought from Egypt and Sudan
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <i>
         Crypte aux étoiles
        </i>
        ("star
        <a href="/wiki/Crypt" title="Crypt">
         crypt
        </a>
        ") is situated in the vaulted basement below the
        <a href="/wiki/Observatory_of_Strasbourg" title="Observatory of Strasbourg">
         Observatory of Strasbourg
        </a>
        and displays old telescopes and other antique astronomical devices such as clocks and
        <a href="/wiki/Theodolite" title="Theodolite">
         theodolites
        </a>
        .
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_in_the_suburbs">
        Museums in the suburbs
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Museums in the suburbs">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <i>
         Musée Les Secrets du Chocolat
        </i>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Chocolate" title="Chocolate">
         Chocolate
        </a>
        museum) in
        <a href="/wiki/Geispolsheim" title="Geispolsheim">
         Geispolsheim
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
         <a href="#cite_note-31">
          [31]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Fr%C3%A8re&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fort Frère (page does not exist)">
         Fort Frère
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Oberhausbergen" title="Oberhausbergen">
         Oberhausbergen
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
         <a href="#cite_note-32">
          [32]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Fort_Rapp" title="Fort Rapp">
         Fort Rapp
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Reichstett" title="Reichstett">
         Reichstett
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         Pixel Museum
        </i>
        , a
        <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">
         video game
        </a>
        museum, in
        <a href="/wiki/Schiltigheim" title="Schiltigheim">
         Schiltigheim
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
         <a href="#cite_note-33">
          [33]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         MM Park France
        </i>
        , a military museum, in
        <a href="/wiki/La_Wantzenau" title="La Wantzenau">
         La Wantzenau
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
         <a href="#cite_note-34">
          [34]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demographics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg">
          <img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>
         </a>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          <b>
           This section needs expansion
          </b>
          .
          <small>
           You can help by
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">
            adding to it
           </a>
           .
          </small>
          <small>
           <i>
            (June 2017)
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Urban_area_(France)" title="Urban area (France)">
        metropolitan area
       </a>
       of Strasbourg had a population of 768,868 inhabitants in 2012 (French side of the border only), while the transnational
       <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg-Ortenau_Eurodistrict" title="Strasbourg-Ortenau Eurodistrict">
        Eurodistrict
       </a>
       had a population of 915,000 inhabitants in 2014.
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Strasbourg is the seat of internationally renowned institutions of music and drama:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Orchestre_philharmonique_de_Strasbourg" title="Orchestre philharmonique de Strasbourg">
         Orchestre philharmonique de Strasbourg
        </a>
        , founded in 1855, one of the oldest symphonic orchestras in western Europe. Based since 1975 in the
        <a href="/wiki/Palais_de_la_musique_et_des_congr%C3%A8s" title="Palais de la musique et des congrès">
         Palais de la musique et des congrès
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Op%C3%A9ra_national_du_Rhin" title="Opéra national du Rhin">
         Opéra national du Rhin
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_national_de_Strasbourg" title="Théâtre national de Strasbourg">
         Théâtre national de Strasbourg
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Percussions_de_Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Percussions de Strasbourg (page does not exist)">
         Percussions de Strasbourg
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_du_Maillon&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Théâtre du Maillon (page does not exist)">
         Théâtre du Maillon
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        The "
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Laiterie&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Laiterie (page does not exist)">
         Laiterie
        </a>
        "
       </li>
       <li>
        Joshy's house - a venue for performance poetry and freestyle urban music.
       </li>
       <li>
        Au Zénith
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Other theatres are the
       <i>
        Théâtre jeune public
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        TAPS Scala
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        Kafteur
       </i>
       ...
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Events">
        Events
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Events">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Musica_(French_music_festival)" title="Musica (French music festival)">
         Musica
        </a>
        , international festival of contemporary classical music (autumn)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg_Music_Festival" title="Strasbourg Music Festival">
         Festival international de Strasbourg
        </a>
        (founded in 1932), festival of classical music and
        <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">
         jazz
        </a>
        (summer)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Festival_des_Artefacts&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Festival des Artefacts (page does not exist)">
         Festival des Artefacts
        </a>
        , festival of contemporary non-classical music
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Les_Nuits_%C3%A9lectroniques_de_l%27Ososph%C3%A8re&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Les Nuits électroniques de l'Ososphère (page does not exist)">
         Les Nuits électroniques de l'Ososphère
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Spectre_Film_Festival" title="Spectre Film Festival">
         Spectre Film Festival
        </a>
        is an annual
        <a href="/wiki/Film_festival" title="Film festival">
         film festival
        </a>
        that is devoted to science fiction,
        <a href="/wiki/Horror_film" title="Horror film">
         horror
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Fantasy" title="Fantasy">
         fantasy
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_Strasbourg_International_Film_Festival&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The Strasbourg International Film Festival (page does not exist)">
         The Strasbourg International Film Festival
        </a>
        is an annual film festival focusing on new and emerging
        <a href="/wiki/Independent_film" title="Independent film">
         independent filmmakers
        </a>
        from around the world.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Universities_and_tertiary_education">
        Universities and tertiary education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Universities and tertiary education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Strasbourg, well known as centre of
       <a href="/wiki/Humanism" title="Humanism">
        humanism
       </a>
       , has a long history of excellence in higher-education, at the crossroads of French and German intellectual traditions. Although Strasbourg had been annexed by the Kingdom of France in 1683, it still remained connected to the German-speaking intellectual world throughout the 18th century and the university attracted numerous students from the
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">
        Holy Roman Empire
       </a>
       , including
       <a href="/wiki/Johann_Wolfgang_von_Goethe" title="Johann Wolfgang von Goethe">
        Goethe
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Klemens_Wenzel,_Prince_von_Metternich" title="Klemens Wenzel, Prince von Metternich">
        Metternich
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_von_Montgelas" title="Maximilian von Montgelas">
        Montgelas
       </a>
       , who studied law in Strasbourg, among the most prominent. Nowadays, Strasbourg is known to offer among the best university courses in France, after Paris.
      </p>
      <p>
       Up until January 2009 there were three
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Strasbourg" title="University of Strasbourg">
        universities in Strasbourg
       </a>
       , with an approximate total of 48,500 students as of 2007
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (another 4,500 students are being taught at one of the diverse
       <a href="/wiki/Postgraduate_education" title="Postgraduate education">
        post-graduate
       </a>
       schools):
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Strasbourg I –
        <a href="/wiki/Louis_Pasteur_University" title="Louis Pasteur University">
         Louis Pasteur University
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Strasbourg II –
        <a href="/wiki/Marc_Bloch_University" title="Marc Bloch University">
         Marc Bloch University
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Strasbourg III –
        <a href="/wiki/Robert_Schuman_University" title="Robert Schuman University">
         Robert Schuman University
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Since 1 January 2009, those three universities have merged and constitute now the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_de_Strasbourg" title="Université de Strasbourg">
        Université de Strasbourg
       </a>
       . Schools part of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_de_Strasbourg" title="Université de Strasbourg">
        Université de Strasbourg
       </a>
       include:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The IEP (
        <a href="/wiki/Institut_d%27%C3%A9tudes_politiques_de_Strasbourg" title="Institut d'études politiques de Strasbourg">
         Institut d'études politiques de Strasbourg
        </a>
        ), the University of Strasbourg's political science &amp; international studies center.
       </li>
       <li>
        The EMS (
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_de_management_Strasbourg" title="École de management Strasbourg">
         École de management Strasbourg
        </a>
        ), the University of Strasbourg's Business School.
       </li>
       <li>
        The INSA (
        <a href="/wiki/Institut_national_des_sciences_appliqu%C3%A9es" title="Institut national des sciences appliquées">
         Institut national des sciences appliquées
        </a>
        ), the University of Strasbourg's Engineering School.
       </li>
       <li>
        The ENA (
        <a href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_nationale_d%27administration" title="École nationale d'administration">
         École nationale d'administration
        </a>
        ). ENA trains most of the nation's high-ranking civil servants. The relocation to Strasbourg was meant to give a European vocation to the school and to implement the French government's "décentralisation" plan.
       </li>
       <li>
        The ESAD (
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%89cole_sup%C3%A9rieure_des_arts_d%C3%A9coratifs&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="École supérieure des arts décoratifs (page does not exist)">
         École supérieure des arts décoratifs
        </a>
        ) is an
        <a href="/wiki/Art_school" title="Art school">
         art school
        </a>
        of European reputation.
       </li>
       <li>
        The ISEG Group (
        <a href="/wiki/Institut_sup%C3%A9rieur_europ%C3%A9en_de_gestion_group" title="Institut supérieur européen de gestion group">
         Institut supérieur européen de gestion group
        </a>
        ).
       </li>
       <li>
        The ISU (
        <a href="/wiki/International_Space_University" title="International Space University">
         International Space University
        </a>
        ) is located in the south of Strasbourg (
        <a href="/wiki/Illkirch-Graffenstaden" title="Illkirch-Graffenstaden">
         Illkirch-Graffenstaden
        </a>
        ).
       </li>
       <li>
        The ECPM (
        <a href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_europ%C3%A9enne_de_chimie,_polym%C3%A8res_et_mat%C3%A9riaux" title="École européenne de chimie, polymères et matériaux">
         École européenne de chimie, polymères et matériaux
        </a>
        ).
       </li>
       <li>
        The ENSIIE (
        <a href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_nationale_sup%C3%A9rieure_d%27informatique_pour_l%27industrie_et_l%27entreprise" title="École nationale supérieure d'informatique pour l'industrie et l'entreprise">
         École nationale supérieure d'informatique pour l'industrie et l'entreprise
        </a>
        ).
       </li>
       <li>
        The EPITA (
        <a href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_pour_l%27informatique_et_les_techniques_avanc%C3%A9es" title="École pour l'informatique et les techniques avancées">
         École pour l'informatique et les techniques avancées
        </a>
        ).
       </li>
       <li>
        The EPITECH (
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_pour_l%27informatique_et_les_nouvelles_technologies" title="École pour l'informatique et les nouvelles technologies">
         École pour l'informatique et les nouvelles technologies
        </a>
        ).
       </li>
       <li>
        The INET (
        <a href="/wiki/Institut_national_des_%C3%A9tudes_territoriales" title="Institut national des études territoriales">
         Institut national des études territoriales
        </a>
        ).
       </li>
       <li>
        The IIEF (
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Institut_international_d%27%C3%A9tudes_fran%C3%A7aises&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Institut international d'études françaises (page does not exist)">
         Institut international d'études françaises
        </a>
        ).
       </li>
       <li>
        The ENGEES (
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%89cole_nationale_du_g%C3%A9nie_de_l%27eau_et_de_l%27environnement_de_Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="École nationale du génie de l'eau et de l'environnement de Strasbourg (page does not exist)">
         École nationale du génie de l'eau et de l'environnement de Strasbourg
        </a>
        ).
       </li>
       <li>
        The CUEJ (
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Centre_universitaire_d%27enseignement_du_journalisme&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Centre universitaire d'enseignement du journalisme (page does not exist)">
         Centre universitaire d'enseignement du journalisme
        </a>
        ).
       </li>
       <li>
        TÉLÉCOM Physique Strasbourg,(
        <a href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_nationale_sup%C3%A9rieure_de_physique_de_Strasbourg" title="École nationale supérieure de physique de Strasbourg">
         École nationale supérieure de physique de Strasbourg
        </a>
        ), Institute of Technology, located in the South of Strasbourg (Illkirch-Graffenstaden).
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>

       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

       International schools include:

        </a>
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lyc%C3%A9e_international_des_Pontonniers" title="fr:Lycée international des Pontonniers">
