      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">
        Libraries
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Libraries">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Absolute_Bibliotheque_nationale_01.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Absolute_Bibliotheque_nationale_01.jpg/220px-Absolute_Bibliotheque_nationale_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Absolute_Bibliotheque_nationale_01.jpg/330px-Absolute_Bibliotheque_nationale_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Absolute_Bibliotheque_nationale_01.jpg/440px-Absolute_Bibliotheque_nationale_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Absolute_Bibliotheque_nationale_01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Lateral view of the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biblioth%C3%A8que_nationale_et_universitaire" title="Bibliothèque nationale et universitaire">
          National Library
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biblioth%C3%A8que_nationale_et_universitaire" title="Bibliothèque nationale et universitaire">
        Bibliothèque nationale et universitaire
       </a>
       (BNU) is, with its collection of more than 3,000,000 titles,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the second largest library in France after the
       <a href="/wiki/Biblioth%C3%A8que_nationale_de_France" title="Bibliothèque nationale de France">
        Bibliothèque nationale de France
       </a>
       . It was founded by the German administration after the complete destruction of the previous municipal library in 1871 and holds the unique status of being simultaneously a students' and a national library. The Strasbourg municipal library had been marked erroneously as "City Hall" in a French commercial map, which had been captured and used by the German artillery to lay their guns. A librarian from Munich later pointed out "...that the destruction of the precious collection was not the fault of a German artillery officer, who used the French map, but of the slovenly and inaccurate scholarship of a Frenchman."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Butler,_Pierce_1945._Page_15_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Butler,_Pierce_1945._Page_15-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The municipal library Bibliothèque municipale de Strasbourg (BMS) administrates a network of ten medium-sized librairies in different areas of the town. A six stories high "Grande bibliothèque", the
       <i>
        Médiathèque
        <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Malraux" title="André Malraux">
         André Malraux
        </a>
       </i>
       , was inaugurated on 19 September 2008 and is considered the largest in Eastern France.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Incunabula">
        Incunabula
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Incunabula">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       As one of the earliest centers of book-printing in Europe (see above: History), Strasbourg for a long time held a large number of
       <a href="/wiki/Incunable" title="Incunable">
        incunabula
       </a>
       —documents printed before 1500—in her library as one of her most precious heritages. After the total destruction of this institution in 1870, however, a new collection had to be reassembled from scratch. Today, Strasbourg's different public and institutional libraries again display a sizable total number of incunabula, distributed as follows:
       <i>
        Bibliothèque nationale et universitaire
       </i>
       , ca. 2 098
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        Médiathèque de la ville et de la communauté urbaine de Strasbourg
       </i>
       , 394
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        Bibliothèque du Grand Séminaire
       </i>
       , 238
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        Médiathèque protestante
       </i>
       , 94
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <i>
        Bibliothèque alsatique du Crédit Mutuel
       </i>
       , 5.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
        Transportation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Transportation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Strasbourg_PontTh%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_02.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Strasbourg_PontTh%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_02.JPG/220px-Strasbourg_PontTh%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_02.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Strasbourg_PontTh%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_02.JPG/330px-Strasbourg_PontTh%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Strasbourg_PontTh%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_02.JPG/440px-Strasbourg_PontTh%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_02.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Strasbourg_PontTh%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_02.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         One of Strasbourg's trams passes over one of its canals, whilst a tourist trip boat passes underneath
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Train services operate from the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gare_de_Strasbourg" title="Gare de Strasbourg">
         Gare de Strasbourg
        </a>
       </i>
       , the city's main station in the city centre, eastward to
       <a href="/wiki/Offenburg" title="Offenburg">
        Offenburg
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Karlsruhe" title="Karlsruhe">
        Karlsruhe
       </a>
       in Germany, westward to
       <a href="/wiki/Metz" title="Metz">
        Metz
       </a>
       and Paris, and southward to
       <a href="/wiki/Basel" title="Basel">
        Basel
       </a>
       . Strasbourg's links with the rest of France have improved due to its recent connection to the
       <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">
        TGV
       </a>
       network, with the first phase of the
       <a href="/wiki/LGV_Est" title="LGV Est">
        TGV
        <i>
         Est
        </i>
       </a>
       (Paris–Strasbourg) in 2007, the
       <a href="/wiki/LGV_Rhin-Rh%C3%B4ne" title="LGV Rhin-Rhône">
        TGV
        <i>
         Rhin-Rhône
        </i>
       </a>
       (Strasbourg-
       <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">
        Lyon
       </a>
       ) in 2012, and the second phase of the TGV Est in July 2016.
      </p>
      <p>
       Strasbourg also has its
       <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg_Airport" title="Strasbourg Airport">
        own airport
       </a>
       , serving major domestic destinations as well as international destinations in Europe and
       <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">
        northern Africa
       </a>
       . The airport is linked to the
       <i>
        Gare de Strasbourg
       </i>
       by a frequent train service.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       City transportation in Strasbourg includes the futurist-looking
       <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg_tramway" title="Strasbourg tramway">
        Strasbourg tramway
       </a>
       that opened in 1994 and is operated by the regional transit company
       <a href="/wiki/Compagnie_des_Transports_Strasbourgeois" title="Compagnie des Transports Strasbourgeois">
        Compagnie des Transports Strasbourgeois
       </a>
       (CTS), consisting of 6 lines with a total length of 55.8 km (34.7 mi). The CTS also operates a comprehensive bus network throughout the city that is integrated with the trams. With more than 500 km (311 mi) of bicycle paths, biking in the city is convenient and the CTS operates a cheap
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bike-sharing" title="Bike-sharing">
        bike-sharing
       </a>
       scheme named
       <i>
        Vélhop'
       </i>
       . The CTS, and its predecessors, also operated a previous generation of
       <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">
        tram
       </a>
       system between 1878 and 1960, complemented by
       <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">
        trolleybus
       </a>
       routes between 1939 and 1962.
      </p>
      <p>
       Being a city on the
       <a href="/wiki/Ill_(France)" title="Ill (France)">
        Ill
       </a>
       and close to the
       <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">
        Rhine
       </a>
       , Strasbourg has always been an important centre of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fluvial_navigation" title="Fluvial navigation">
        fluvial navigation
       </a>
       , as is attested by archeological findings. In 1682 the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Canal_de_la_Bruche" title="Canal de la Bruche">
         Canal de la Bruche
        </a>
       </i>
       was added to the river navigations, initially to provide transport for
       <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">
        sandstone
       </a>
       from quarries in the
       <a href="/wiki/Vosges" title="Vosges">
        Vosges
       </a>
       for use in the fortification of the city. That canal has since closed, but the subsequent
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canal_du_Rhone_au_Rhine" title="Canal du Rhone au Rhine">
         Canal du Rhone au Rhine
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canal_de_la_Marne_au_Rhin" title="Canal de la Marne au Rhin">
         Canal de la Marne au Rhin
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Grand_Canal_d%27Alsace" title="Grand Canal d'Alsace">
         Grand Canal d'Alsace
        </a>
       </i>
       are still in use, as is the important activity of the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port_autonome_de_Strasbourg" title="Port autonome de Strasbourg">
         Port autonome de Strasbourg
        </a>
       </i>
       . Water tourism inside the city proper attracts hundreds of thousands of tourists yearly.
      </p>
      <p>
       The tram system that now criss-crosses the historic city centre complements walking and biking in it. The centre has been transformed into a pedestrian priority zone that enables and invites walking and biking by making these active modes of transport comfortable, safe and enjoyable. These attributes are accomplished by applying the principle of
       <a href="/wiki/Permeability_(spatial_and_transport_planning)" title="Permeability (spatial and transport planning)">
        "filtered permeability"
       </a>
       to the existing irregular network of streets. It means that the network adaptations favour active transportation and, selectively, "filter out" the car by reducing the number of streets that run through the centre. While certain streets are discontinuous for cars, they connect to a network of pedestrian and bike paths which permeate the entire centre. In addition, these paths go through public squares and open spaces increasing the enjoyment of the trip. This logic of filtering a mode of transport is fully expressed in a comprehensive model for laying out neighbourhoods and districts – the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fused_Grid" title="Fused Grid">
        Fused Grid
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       At present the
       <a href="/wiki/A35_autoroute" title="A35 autoroute">
        A35 autoroute
       </a>
       , which parallels the Rhine between
       <a href="/wiki/Karlsruhe" title="Karlsruhe">
        Karlsruhe
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Basel" title="Basel">
        Basel
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/A4_autoroute" title="A4 autoroute">
        A4 autoroute
       </a>
       , which links
       <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">
        Paris
       </a>
       with Strasbourg, penetrate close to the centre of the city. The
       <i>
        Grand contournement ouest
       </i>
       (GCO) project, programmed since 1999, plans to construct a 24-kilometre-long (15 mi) highway connection between the junctions of the A4 and the A35 autoroutes in the north and of the A35 and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=A352_autoroute&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="A352 autoroute (page does not exist)">
        A352
       </a>
       autoroutes in the south. This routes well to the west of the city and is meant to divest a significant portion of motorized traffic from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unit%C3%A9_urbaine" title="Unité urbaine">
        unité urbaine
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Strasbourg_Public_Transportation_Statistics">
        Strasbourg Public Transportation Statistics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Strasbourg Public Transportation Statistics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The average amount of time people spend commuting with public transit in Strasbourg, for example to and from work, on a weekday is 52 min. 7% of public transit riders, ride for more than 2 hours every day. The average amount of time people wait at a stop or station for public transit is 9 min, while 11% of riders wait for over 20 minutes on average every day. The average distance people usually ride in a single trip with public transit is 3.9 km, while 0% travel for over 12 km in a single direction.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="European_role">
        European role
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: European role">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Council_of_Europe_Palais_de_l%27Europe_aerial_view.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1878" data-file-width="2835" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Council_of_Europe_Palais_de_l%27Europe_aerial_view.JPG/220px-Council_of_Europe_Palais_de_l%27Europe_aerial_view.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Council_of_Europe_Palais_de_l%27Europe_aerial_view.JPG/330px-Council_of_Europe_Palais_de_l%27Europe_aerial_view.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Council_of_Europe_Palais_de_l%27Europe_aerial_view.JPG/440px-Council_of_Europe_Palais_de_l%27Europe_aerial_view.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">

          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Europe" title="Palace of Europe">
          Palace of Europe
         </a>
         of the
         <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">
          Council of Europe
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Institutions">
        Institutions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Institutions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Institutions_in_Strasbourg" title="European Institutions in Strasbourg">
        European Institutions in Strasbourg
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Strasbourg is the seat of over twenty international institutions,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       most famously of the
       <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">
        Council of Europe
       </a>
       and of the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">
        European Parliament
       </a>
       , of which it is the
       <a href="/wiki/Seat_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Strasbourg" title="Seat of the European Parliament in Strasbourg">
        official seat
       </a>
       . Strasbourg is considered the legislative and democratic capital of the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       , while
       <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">
        Brussels
       </a>
       is considered the executive and administrative capital and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luxembourg_(city)" title="Luxembourg (city)">
        Luxembourg
       </a>
       the judiciary and
       <a href="/wiki/Financial_capital" title="Financial capital">
        financial capital
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Strasbourg is the seat of the following organisations, among others:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Central_Commission_for_Navigation_on_the_Rhine" title="Central Commission for Navigation on the Rhine">
         Central Commission for Navigation on the Rhine
        </a>
        (since 1920)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">
         Council of Europe
        </a>
        with all the bodies and organisations affiliated to this institution (since 1949)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">
         European Parliament
        </a>
        (since 1952)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/European_Ombudsman" title="European Ombudsman">
         European Ombudsman
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Eurocorps" title="Eurocorps">
         Eurocorps
        </a>
        headquarters,
       </li>
       <li>
        Franco-German television channel
        <a href="/wiki/Arte" title="Arte">
         Arte
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/European_Science_Foundation" title="European Science Foundation">
         European Science Foundation
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/International_Institute_of_Human_Rights" title="International Institute of Human Rights">
         International Institute of Human Rights
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Human_Frontier_Science_Program" title="Human Frontier Science Program">
         Human Frontier Science Program
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/International_Commission_on_Civil_Status" title="International Commission on Civil Status">
         International Commission on Civil Status
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_European_Regions" title="Assembly of European Regions">
         Assembly of European Regions
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/University_of_Strasbourg" title="University of Strasbourg">
         Centre for European Studies
        </a>
        (French:
        <i>
         Centre d'études européennes de Strasbourg
        </i>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Sakharov_Prize" title="Sakharov Prize">
         Sakharov Prize
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Eurodistrict">
        Eurodistrict
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Eurodistrict">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg-Ortenau_Eurodistrict" title="Strasbourg-Ortenau Eurodistrict">
        Strasbourg-Ortenau Eurodistrict
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       France and Germany have created a
       <a href="/wiki/Eurodistrict" title="Eurodistrict">
        Eurodistrict
       </a>
       straddling the Rhine, combining the Greater Strasbourg and the
       <a href="/wiki/Ortenaukreis" title="Ortenaukreis">
        Ortenau
       </a>
       district of
       <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">
        Baden-Württemberg
       </a>
       , with some common administration. It was established in 2005 and is fully functional since 2010.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stade_de_la_Meinau.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="298" data-file-width="500" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Stade_de_la_Meinau.JPG/220px-Stade_de_la_Meinau.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Stade_de_la_Meinau.JPG/330px-Stade_de_la_Meinau.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Stade_de_la_Meinau.JPG/440px-Stade_de_la_Meinau.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stade_de_la_Meinau.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Stade_de_la_Meinau" title="Stade de la Meinau">
          Stade de la Meinau
         </a>
         , home of
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RC_Strasbourg" title="RC Strasbourg">
          RC Strasbourg
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Sporting teams from Strasbourg are the
       <a href="/wiki/RC_Strasbourg_Alsace" title="RC Strasbourg Alsace">
        Racing Club de Strasbourg Alsace
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">
        football
       </a>
       ),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strasbourg_IG" title="Strasbourg IG">
        Strasbourg IG
       </a>
       (basketball) and the
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%89toile_Noire_de_Strasbourg" title="Étoile Noire de Strasbourg">
        Étoile Noire
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">
        ice hockey
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The women's tennis
       <a href="/wiki/Internationaux_de_Strasbourg" title="Internationaux de Strasbourg">
        Internationaux de Strasbourg
       </a>
       is one of the most important French tournaments of its kind outside
       <a href="/wiki/French_Open" title="French Open">
        Roland-Garros
       </a>
       . In 1922, Strasbourg was the venue for the XVI Grand Prix de l’A.C.F. which saw Fiat battle Bugatti, Ballot, Rolland Pilain, and Britain's Aston Martin and
       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Prix_Sunbeams_1922" title="Grand Prix Sunbeams 1922">
        Sunbeam
       </a>
       .
      </p>

       </li>

       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Georg_Simmel" title="Georg Simmel">
        Georg Simmel
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Albert_Schweitzer" title="Albert Schweitzer">
        Albert Schweitzer
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Otto_Klemperer" title="Otto Klemperer">
        Otto Klemperer
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Marc_Bloch" title="Marc Bloch">
        Marc Bloch
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Fujimori" title="Alberto Fujimori">
        Alberto Fujimori
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Marjane_Satrapi" title="Marjane Satrapi">
        Marjane Satrapi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Paul_Ric%C5%93ur" title="Paul Ricœur">
        Paul Ricoeur
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Jean-Marie_Lehn" title="Jean-Marie Lehn">
        Jean-Marie Lehn
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">
        Twin towns and sister cities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Twin towns and sister cities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_France" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in France">
        List of twin towns and sister cities in France
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Strasbourg is
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Town_twinning" title="Town twinning">
        twinned
       </a>
       with:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Strasbourg_twinnings_54-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Strasbourg_twinnings-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <span class="flagicon">
         <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
          <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
         </a>
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">
         Boston
        </a>
        , United States, since 1960
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Strasbourg_twinnings_54-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-Strasbourg_twinnings-54">
          [54]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boston_sisters_55-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Boston_sisters-55">
          [55]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="flagicon">
         <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
          <img alt="United Kingdom" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
         </a>
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Leicester" title="Leicester">
         Leicester
        </a>
        , United Kingdom, since 1960
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Strasbourg_twinnings_54-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-Strasbourg_twinnings-54">
          [54]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Archant_twinning_56-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Archant_twinning-56">
          [56]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leicester_twinnings_57-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Leicester_twinnings-57">
          [57]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="flagicon">
         <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">
          <img alt="Germany" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
         </a>
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">
         Stuttgart
        </a>
        , Germany, since 1962
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Strasbourg_twinnings_54-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-Strasbourg_twinnings-54">
          [54]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stuttgart_twinnings_58-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Stuttgart_twinnings-58">
          [58]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="flagicon">
         <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">
          <img alt="Germany" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
         </a>
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">
         Dresden
        </a>
        , Germany, since 1990
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Strasbourg_twinnings_54-4">
         <a href="#cite_note-Strasbourg_twinnings-54">
          [54]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dresden_59-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Dresden-59">
          [59]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="flagicon">
         <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
          <img alt="Israel" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="660" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/21px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/32px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/41px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png 2x" width="21"/>
         </a>
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Ramat_Gan" title="Ramat Gan">
         Ramat Gan
        </a>
        , Israel, since 1991
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Strasbourg_twinnings_54-5">
         <a href="#cite_note-Strasbourg_twinnings-54">
          [54]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ramat_Gan_twinnings_60-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Ramat_Gan_twinnings-60">
          [60]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Strasbourg has cooperative agreements with:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Jacmel" title="Jacmel">
         Jacmel
        </a>
        , Haiti, since 1996 (Coopération décentralisée)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Veliky_Novgorod" title="Veliky Novgorod">
         Veliky Novgorod
        </a>
        , Russia, since 1997 (Coopération décentralisée)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fes" title="Fes">
         Fes
        </a>
        , Morocco (Coopération décentralisée)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Douala" title="Douala">
         Douala
        </a>
        , Cameroon (Coopération décentralisée)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Bamako" title="Bamako">
         Bamako
        </a>
        , Mali (Coopération décentralisée)
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">
        In popular culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: In popular culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="In_film">
        In film
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: In film">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The opening scenes of the 1977
        <a href="/wiki/Ridley_Scott" title="Ridley Scott">
         Ridley Scott
        </a>
        film
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/The_Duellists" title="The Duellists">
          The Duellists
         </a>
        </i>
        take place in Strasbourg in 1800.
       </li>
       <li>
        The 2007 film
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/In_the_City_of_Sylvia" title="In the City of Sylvia">
          In the City of Sylvia
         </a>
        </i>
        is set in Strasbourg.
       </li>
       <li>
        Early February 2011, principal photography for
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Sherlock_Holmes:_A_Game_of_Shadows" title="Sherlock Holmes: A Game of Shadows">
          Sherlock Holmes: A Game of Shadows
         </a>
        </i>
        (2011) moved for two days to Strasbourg. Shooting took place on, around, and inside the Strasbourg Cathedral. The opening scene of the movie covers an assassination-bombing in the city.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="In_literature">
        In literature
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: In literature">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        One of the longest chapters of
        <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Sterne" title="Laurence Sterne">
         Laurence Sterne
        </a>
        's novel
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/The_Life_and_Opinions_of_Tristram_Shandy,_Gentleman" title="The Life and Opinions of Tristram Shandy, Gentleman">
          Tristram Shandy
         </a>
        </i>
        (1759–1767), "
        <a href="/wiki/Hafen_Slawkenbergius" title="Hafen Slawkenbergius">
         Slawkenbergius
        </a>
        ' tale", takes place in Strasbourg.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
         <a href="#cite_note-61">
          [61]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        An episode of
        <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Lewis_(writer)" title="Matthew Lewis (writer)">
         Matthew Gregory Lewis
        </a>
        ' novel
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/The_Monk" title="The Monk">
          The Monk
         </a>
        </i>
        (1796) takes place in the forests then surrounding Strasbourg.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="In_music">
        In music
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: In music">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">
         Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart
        </a>
        called his
        <a href="/wiki/Violin_Concerto_No._3_(Mozart)" title="Violin Concerto No. 3 (Mozart)">
         Third violin concerto
        </a>
        (1775)
        <i>
         Straßburger Konzert
        </i>
        because of one of its most prominent
        <a href="/wiki/Motif_(music)" title="Motif (music)">
         motives
        </a>
        , based on a local,
        <a href="/wiki/Minuet" title="Minuet">
         minuet
        </a>
        -like dance that had already appeared as a tune in a symphony by
        <a href="/wiki/Carl_Ditters_von_Dittersdorf" title="Carl Ditters von Dittersdorf">
         Carl Ditters von Dittersdorf
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
         <a href="#cite_note-62">
          [62]
         </a>
        </sup>
        It is not related to Mozart's ulterior stay in Strasbourg (1778), where he gave three concert performances on the piano.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Havergal_Brian" title="Havergal Brian">
         Havergal Brian
        </a>
        's Symphony No.7 was inspired by passages in Goethe's memoirs recalling his time spent at Strasbourg University. The work ends with an orchestral bell sounding the note E, the strike-note of the bell of Strasbourg Cathedral.
       </li>
       <li>
        British
        <a href="/wiki/Art_punk" title="Art punk">
         art-punk
        </a>
        band
        <a href="/wiki/The_Rakes" title="The Rakes">
         The Rakes
        </a>
        had a minor hit in 2005 with their song "Strasbourg". This song features witty lyrics with themes of espionage and vodka and includes a cleverly placed count of 'eins, zwei, drei, vier!!', even though Strasbourg's
        <a href="/wiki/Spoken_language" title="Spoken language">
         spoken language
        </a>
        is French.
       </li>
       <li>
        On their 1974 album
        <i>
         Hamburger Concerto
        </i>
        , Dutch progressive band
        <a href="/wiki/Focus_(band)" title="Focus (band)">
         Focus
        </a>
        included a track called "La Cathédrale de Strasbourg", which included chimes from a cathedral-like bell.
       </li>
       <li>
        Strasbourg pie, a dish containing
        <a href="/wiki/Foie_gras#Cold_preparations" title="Foie gras">
         foie gras
        </a>
        , is mentioned in the finale of the
        <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Lloyd_Webber" title="Andrew Lloyd Webber">
         Andrew Lloyd Webber
        </a>
        musical
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Cats_(musical)" title="Cats (musical)">
          Cats
         </a>
        </i>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Several works have specifically been dedicated to Strasbourg Cathedral, notably
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Ad_hoc" title="Ad hoc">
          ad hoc
         </a>
        </i>
        compositions (
        <a href="/wiki/Mass_(music)" title="Mass (music)">
         masses
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Motet" title="Motet">
         motets
        </a>
        etc.) by
        <a href="/wiki/Kapellmeister" title="Kapellmeister">
         Kapellmeisters
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Franz_Xaver_Richter" title="Franz Xaver Richter">
         Franz Xaver Richter
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Ignaz_Pleyel" title="Ignaz Pleyel">
         Ignaz Pleyel
        </a>
        and, more recently,
        <i>
         It is Finished
        </i>
        by
        <a href="/wiki/John_Tavener" title="John Tavener">
         John Tavener
        </a>
        .
       </li>
      </ul>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sources">
        Sources
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strasbourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Sources">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <i>
         Connaître Strasbourg
        </i>
        by Roland Recht, Georges Foessel and Jean-Pierre Klein, 1988,
        <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
         ISBN
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/2-7032-0185-0" title="Special:BookSources/2-7032-0185-0">
         2-7032-0185-0
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         Histoire de Strasbourg des origines à nos jours
        </i>
        , four volumes (ca. 2000 pages) by a collective of historians under the guidance of Georges Livet and Francis Rapp, 1982,
        <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
         ISBN
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/2-7165-0041-X" title="Special:BookSources/2-7165-0041-X">
         2-7165-0041-X
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
